  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7763d906-ddcc-4d35-8d09-9685499570fc'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer17554124559147577494">With every end comes a new beginning in the fourth installment of Soman Chainani’s New York Times bestselling School for Good and Evil series, Quests for Glory. Join Sophie, Agatha, Tedros, and the other students as they begin a new era in the Endless Woods—The Camelot Years—where Evers and Nevers alike must move beyond the bounds of school and into the biggest, boldest ad</span>
  <span id="freeText17554124559147577494" style="display:none">With every end comes a new beginning in the fourth installment of Soman Chainani’s New York Times bestselling School for Good and Evil series, Quests for Glory. Join Sophie, Agatha, Tedros, and the other students as they begin a new era in the Endless Woods—The Camelot Years—where Evers and Nevers alike must move beyond the bounds of school and into the biggest, boldest adventures of their lives.<br /><br />The students at the School for Good and Evil thought they had found their final Ever After when they vanquished the malevolent School Master. Now, on their required fourth-year quests, the students face obstacles both dangerous and unpredictable, and the stakes are high: success brings eternal adoration, and failure means obscurity forever.<br /><br />For their quests, Agatha and Tedros are trying to return Camelot to its former splendor as queen and king. For her quest, Dean Sophie seeks to mold Evil in her own image. But soon they all feel themselves growing more isolated and alone. When their classmates’ quests plunge into chaos, however, someone must lead the charge to save them...</span>

<div id="review_1747491939" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1747491939" />
    <a title="Ramona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52524382-ramona"><img alt="Ramona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604282330p2/52524382.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1747491939?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ramona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ramona" href="/user/show/52524382-ramona">Ramona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062658470" href="/book/show/32711417-quests-for-glory">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1747491939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16715658287556819973">Oh boy... Why couldn’t we have just ended with the first trilogy...? *cough* Or better yet, the very first book? *cough* This sequel series is just so unnecessary and so is the new conflict. Also, the multiple POVs were okay, but it felt kind of pointless to put a name at the beginning of each chapter because the style of writing didn’t even change that much.<br/><br/>Whatever. Let me talk about the characters.<br/><br/>Agatha, I will love her and defend her until I die. She doesn’t deserve the hand she’s been deal</span>
  <span id="freeText16715658287556819973" style="display:none">Oh boy... Why couldn’t we have just ended with the first trilogy...? *cough* Or better yet, the very first book? *cough* This sequel series is just so unnecessary and so is the new conflict. Also, the multiple POVs were okay, but it felt kind of pointless to put a name at the beginning of each chapter because the style of writing didn’t even change that much.<br /><br />Whatever. Let me talk about the characters.<br /><br />Agatha, I will love her and defend her until I die. She doesn’t deserve the hand she’s been dealt in life <i>at all</i>. But I guess being awesome gave her good karma at the end because she’s <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the only one who escaped the Snake/Rhian’s Camelot takeover. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The Coven were the best after Agatha, and I ship Willam and Bogden... Wish those two boys got more involvement, though.<br /><br />Tedros, you’re an idiot. #KingAgatha<br /><br />Rhian was a plastic Ken doll and had such bullshit logic when it came to Sophie’s bullshit. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Glad to know he probably faked the whole thing, and I’m not giving up on #Snaric.<br /><br />Oh! Also! The Snake/Rhian = Kei has not died yet and I’m living. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Anyway, author’s favorite Sophie is wicked as usual. Is it the sort of wicked I love? No, I am probably never going to love her or her kind of villain. Sorry, but I’ve never been able to see the appeal of her; I’ve always seen her for everything wrong that she’s done, which is so huge when it comes to her character that I just can’t excuse it in any way, redeeming qualities be damned! But am I glad that it's being acknowledged that she is pure wickedness because c'mon now she's the <i>Dean</i> of Evil? Hell yes. Well, it’s sometimes acknowledged, other times it’s excused, but I’ll take what I can get.<br /><br />The parts where Hort was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[being all possessive and gross with Sophie I was <i>not</i> feeling, and his whole thing with Nicola felt so rushed. Speaking of Nicola, everybody seemed uncharacteristically dumbed down so she could shine as the resident smart one of the group on multiple occasions, which I was <i>also</i> not feeling. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />By the way, I literally gave myself a headache ranting about Hort and Sophie’s BS (both together and apart) to my friend, and got so mad I couldn’t form words when telling the same friend about Agatha constantly being pushed to the side.<br /><br />There are other things that I’d like to say, but honestly I’m exhausted and don’t want to repeat myself. Go read my status updates if you wanna hear all about how I feel about the way Agatha’s treated in the book... and some other things.<br /><br />So. Why did I give this three stars if all I basically did this review was rant? Well, it <i>was</i> enjoyable... mostly. I mean, it was written well and I wasn’t bored, just frustrated. I’m going to read the next book... only because I love this series and am going to see it through to the end, no matter how much it aggravates me.<br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2147274256" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of <u>A Crystal of Time</u></a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2912882857" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of <u>One True King</u></a><br /><br />•••••••••<br /><br /><b>PRE-READ EDIT 6/17/17:</b><br /><br />Y'all, check out <a href="http://ew.com/books/2017/06/14/school-good-evil-quests-glory-trailer-camelot-years/?aal=BdYlejxX3nSfsbQPBFnti1AcwZiGLiPlMIhwbj7YUKJpFGSD" rel="nofollow noopener">the book trailer.</a><br /><br />I'm shook.<br /><br />(Also I swear if Sophie pulls some more shit (cause those chains and lock on her heart have got me suspicious) I will riot for years and you'll never hear the end of it.)<br /><br />•••••••••<br /><br /><b>PRE-READ EDIT 3/3/17:</b><br /><br />LOOK AT THAT COVER!!! DAMN IT'S GORGEOUS!!!<br /><br />IS THAT AGGIE I SEE?!?! IS THAT TEDROS?!?!<br /><br />*squints*<br /><br />Sophie, is that you at the bottom where you belong?<br /><br />Cool, keep doing what you're doing. I couldn't care less.<br /><br />What I do care about is whoever's beside you! Hort (cause he'd naturally be two steps behind)? Anadil (cause that white hair)? Hester (cause maybe she got a haircut)? Some other people? Guess we'll find out in September!<br /><br />*goes back to flipping out*<br /><br />•••••••••<br /><br /><b>PRE-READ EDIT 9/3/16:</b><br /><br />And here, folks, is exactly what I was afraid would happen... I thought everything was all good and happy in the world and that we were DONE WITH AAAAAAALL OF THIS!!!!<br /><br />Still gonna read it though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16715658287556819973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Dorian Jandreau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15202946-dorian-jandreau"><img alt="Dorian Jandreau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546633695p2/15202946.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorian Jandreau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorian Jandreau" href="/user/show/15202946-dorian-jandreau">Dorian Jandreau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062658470" href="/book/show/32711417-quests-for-glory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15202946-dorian-jandreau?shelf=my-biggest-treasures">my-biggest-treasures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15202946-dorian-jandreau?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15202946-dorian-jandreau?shelf=g%C4%97rio-ir-blogio-mokykla">gėrio-ir-blogio-mokykla</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1745714583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2912306370527415420">It‘s always extremely difficult to write reviews of books you love more than life... „<i>Quests for Glory</i>“ is one of them. I‘ve been recommended Soman Chainani from Ever After High doll collector and when I read the first book- I fell in love completely with this author. I understood I found the fantasy world I‘ve been waiting my entire life.<br/><br/>I cannot describe my happiness when I finally got my package from UK (<i>which was taking a lot of time…</i>) and I took this book in my hands. I started reading it i</span>
  <span id="freeText2912306370527415420" style="display:none">It‘s always extremely difficult to write reviews of books you love more than life... „<i>Quests for Glory</i>“ is one of them. I‘ve been recommended Soman Chainani from Ever After High doll collector and when I read the first book- I fell in love completely with this author. I understood I found the fantasy world I‘ve been waiting my entire life.<br /><br />I cannot describe my happiness when I finally got my package from UK (<i>which was taking a lot of time…</i>) and I took this book in my hands. I started reading it immediately. And after reading few chapters I felt how much I want to translate it to Lithuanian. (<i>I translated first chapter and it was a huge challenge</i>) I was very happy to meet Sophie again. (<i>She’s my favorite character because I’m just like her</i>) The author keeps his marvelous style of writing and turning each chapter into “<i>TV-series</i>” that you want to read more and see what happens next. Each chapter is like an episode of fantasy-thriller. Why I love this author so much is because he makes plot twists in each chapter and you can never guess how the entire book will end. He knows how to keep a reader with his story and…then you want MORE. When I noticed his announcement about the 5th book coming in 2018- I was in rainbow-puking-mode. And now when I finished the book- I want a new one RIGHT NOW, because the way it ended makes me lust for “WHAT’S NEXT?!“</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1920387848" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1920387848" />
    <a title="Sabrina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52930632-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554853474p2/52930632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1920387848?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina" href="/user/show/52930632-sabrina">Sabrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062667687" href="/book/show/32711587-quests-for-glory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=hyped-af-to-read">hyped-af-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=illustrated">illustrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=cried-real-tears">cried-real-tears</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52930632-sabrina?shelf=rollercoaster-of-feelings">rollercoaster-of-feelings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1920387848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15411511606262278314"><b>Thriller. Twisting. Hilarious. Relevant. Heart-wrenching. Rollercoaster.</b> These are all words that describe <i>Quests for Glory</i>. <b>I do not say lightly that this is one of the best books I have ever read</b>, especially as the hype for it was astronomical. And boy, did it deliver.<p><b>The standout feature of this book (and series too) is the way it highlights the fluctuating boundaries between Truth and Lies, Good and Evil.</b> It's <a href='http://www.npr.org/2017/09/18/550797568/school-for-good-and-evil-is-a-kids-fantasy-series-for-the-fake-news-era' rel='nofollow noopener'>extremely relevant to today's (and I guess most of history's) political climate</a>. P</p></span>
  <span id="freeText15411511606262278314" style="display:none"><b>Thriller. Twisting. Hilarious. Relevant. Heart-wrenching. Rollercoaster.</b> These are all words that describe <i>Quests for Glory</i>. <b>I do not say lightly that this is one of the best books I have ever read</b>, especially as the hype for it was astronomical. And boy, did it deliver.<p><b>The standout feature of this book (and series too) is the way it highlights the fluctuating boundaries between Truth and Lies, Good and Evil.</b> It's <a href="http://www.npr.org/2017/09/18/550797568/school-for-good-and-evil-is-a-kids-fantasy-series-for-the-fake-news-era" rel="nofollow noopener">extremely relevant to today's (and I guess most of history's) political climate</a>. People like to believe what <i>feels</i> True. Every villain believes they are the hero of their own fairytale.</p><blockquote>
  <i>[B]eware trying to bend the Truth to fit your story instead of facing it head-on. That was your father's mistake. And that's how a Snake becomes a Lion and a Lion becomes a Snake. Because the more you bend the Truth to fit a story, the more it turns into Lies without you even realizing it.</i>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <i>Is it really a Lie if someone is unwilling to see the Truth?</i>
</blockquote><b>I love a book that makes you think, and every book in this series has done so for me.</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16248113.The_School_for_Good_and_Evil__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil___1_" title="The School for Good and Evil (The School for Good and Evil, #1) by Soman Chainani" rel="nofollow noopener">The School for Good and Evil</a> left me questioning Good and Evil, and subverted the sexist tropes of many fairytales. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18172465.A_World_Without_Princes__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil___2_" title="A World Without Princes (The School for Good and Evil, #2) by Soman Chainani" rel="nofollow noopener">A World Without Princes</a> brought discussions about femininity, masculinity and the co-existence of multiple kinds of true love. And <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18004320.The_Last_Ever_After__The_School_for_Good_and_Evil___3_" title="The Last Ever After (The School for Good and Evil, #3) by Soman Chainani" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Ever After</a> highlighted the confusion over what makes a Happy ending happy. Is it you that's Happy? Or what other people expect?<p><b>The second thing I loved was how damn twisty this story was.</b> No one is safe. And the major twist left me REELING. I was actually <i>out of breath</i> from the breakneck pace of the finale. Let's just say I did not know who to trust, and at every turn, Chainani had me second-guessing what I suspected about the Snake and his plans. <b>This twistiness made for some extremely gut-wrenching moments.</b> Two scenes - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Chaddick's *sob* death and Lancelot's (why do I have to grieve here as well as in <i>Merlin</i>) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - I had to actually stop reading and have a moment of silence. I'm still in mourning.</p><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506145593ra/23991437.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435766254ra/15376046.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><b>The characters were so compelling, and the character development as well. Amazing.</b> Special mentions go to the original trio, of course, but also Nicola of Woods Beyond. She is on her way to cementing herself as one of my favourite fictional females of all time! This book was the <b>first in the series with specific character POVs</b>, rather than what was more omniscient narration in the previous trilogy. <b>This succeeded, upped the mystery and suspense, and each character voice was impressively distinct.</b><p>I also <b>liked the increasing diversity</b>, with more characters from what seem to be non-European regions, and also the hint(?!) of a potentially queer pairing (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[William and Bogden <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>), which was an area lacking in the previous three. <b>The humour was class, as always, and the romance was to die for.</b> Hopefully not literally, but from what <i>Quests for Glory</i> was like, I am steeling my Reader heart.</p><b>Very, very impressed.</b> Delivered on everything I'd hoped for and more. Highly, highly recommend!<p>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1556302403?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of <i>The School for Good and Evil</i></a>
</p><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1556684836?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of <i>A World Without Princes</i></a><p>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1556302430?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of <i>The Last Ever After</i></a>
</p></span>

<div id="review_2296992723" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2296992723" />
    <a title="Sara Saif" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33555642-sara-saif"><img alt="Sara Saif" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567114974p2/33555642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2296992723?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara Saif" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara Saif" href="/user/show/33555642-sara-saif">Sara Saif</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33555642-sara-saif?shelf=seriously-so-good-i-can-t-even">seriously-so-good-i-can-t-even</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33555642-sara-saif?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2296992723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11020786562754589261"><p>This isn’t just <i>The School For Good And Evil</i> # 4, it’s a brand new series! Say whaaat? And here little old me read the entire thing thinking it was a standalone. Feeling disoriented right now. Ugh.</p><br/>Let me just say, straight off the bat that even though I wish they had left it alone at the trilogy, this book was spectacular. It was more ambitious and more brutal and more complex and more thrilling than the other ones. They was so much <i>more</i> in it.<br/><p>The mystery was driving me nuts the whole time. Soma</p></span>
  <span id="freeText11020786562754589261" style="display:none"><p>This isn’t just <i>The School For Good And Evil</i> # 4, it’s a brand new series! Say whaaat? And here little old me read the entire thing thinking it was a standalone. Feeling disoriented right now. Ugh.</p><br>Let me just say, straight off the bat that even though I wish they had left it alone at the trilogy, this book was spectacular. It was more ambitious and more brutal and more complex and more thrilling than the other ones. They was so much <i>more</i> in it.<br><p>The mystery was driving me nuts the whole time. Soman Chainani had me guessing and second guessing everyone’s identities, loyalties, motives, intentions. It was <i>intense</i>, yo. The main plot line is SO GOOD. It tops the Good Vs Evil theme by a million percent. I was not expecting that. He trips everything over its head and he does it cleverly.</p><br>The development in this book is glorious, Tedros’s especially. It’s easier to seem perfect and commanding when you don’t have to shoulder the burden of a responsibility, when you do, however, well, that’s when the Truth of your capability becomes clear. Tedros is far, far from being the wise and strong king he always thought he would be. He’s young and naïve and makes lots of mistake. I liked this but it also had me conflicted. I was like, why isn’t he becoming wise and defeating his enemies and taking charge and shit? Then the book ended and I realized this was the first book in a new series. Right. Regardless, I liked the “heroes aren’t always perfect” theme there.<br><p>Sophie too, while being quintessentially Sophie throughout, has grown a lot. She’s more sincere now to everyone around her and I was surprised to find that I didn’t hate her at all. Much.<br>I wish, oh, I wish they had gone a different direction with Hort. I’ve always held a soft spot for him and he feels so used. There’s a scene where he thinks about why he keeps going back to Sophie, how deep down they’re both the same, and that touched me. There was something right about that track if it had been pursued.<br>I like Nicola but she appeared out of nowhere. I previously didn’t give two whits about Chaddick but that changed as well. It’s a well-rounded set of people.</p><br>Despite the fact that it was seen from a million miles, the clever illusions and distractions kept me confused and apprehensive so when the twist did come there was an element of surprise in there. These are the things I would very much like to know in the next books:<br>-What is wrong with Dovey?<br>-What did Lady Gremaine <i>do</i> and why was Arthur writing her letters? Furthermore, where was the fund for Camelot Beautiful even going?<br>-What does Aric have to do with anything?<br>-So Rhian has the Good School Master’s name, and is <i>two</i> people at once? If not, who was the Snake?<br>-The Snake said that he was close to a boy once and that he had thought his happy ending was with a girl? I’m so lost.<br><p> <i>“This is no longer a tale about whether you will find fame or fortune or your perfect little happy ending. This is a tale about whether you are capable of growing from the snake of your own story into the hero of someone else's.”</i></p><br>To sum it up, I enjoyed this <i>vehemently</i>, it turned out to be more serious, intense, mature and tangled up than I expected. <s>Can’t</s> Have to wait for the next one now. Blegh.<br><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518768816ra/25069495.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11020786562754589261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1930896529" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1930896529" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49649873-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541271334p2/49649873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1930896529?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/49649873-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062658470" href="/book/show/32711417-quests-for-glory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49649873-natalie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49649873-natalie?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1930896529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5555910755350613546">I think I’m officially done with this series. I thought the first trilogy was drawn out but this one brings the same issues right back to the front: Agatha and Tedros trusting each other; Agatha and Sophie bickering; the nature of good and evil. <br/><br/>Which would be fine if there hadn’t been 1500 pages said on those subjects in the first 3 books. <br/><br/>The pacing of this book was strange. For example, after a major battle, they all went out on a date to a fancy restaurant. So the plot, which had been exciti</span>
  <span id="freeText5555910755350613546" style="display:none">I think I’m officially done with this series. I thought the first trilogy was drawn out but this one brings the same issues right back to the front: Agatha and Tedros trusting each other; Agatha and Sophie bickering; the nature of good and evil. <br /><br />Which would be fine if there hadn’t been 1500 pages said on those subjects in the first 3 books. <br /><br />The pacing of this book was strange. For example, after a major battle, they all went out on a date to a fancy restaurant. So the plot, which had been exciting, slowed to a snail’s pace as Agatha and Sophie read the restaurant’s menu and gaped over the fancy food. <br /><br />The ending killed it for me. I was contemplating three stars for a while, but the ending - cringeworthy. It was just so obvious. <br /><br />Despite the cliffhanger, I don’t think I’ll continue. I wasn’t over the moon about the series to begin with and I think I like this one the least of the 4. It really should have stayed a trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5555910755350613546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1852686086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1852686086" />
    <a title="Zachary Flye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4584043-zachary-flye"><img alt="Zachary Flye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550284199p2/4584043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1852686086?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zachary Flye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zachary Flye" href="/user/show/4584043-zachary-flye">Zachary Flye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062658470" href="/book/show/32711417-quests-for-glory">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1852686086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16249003575379962937">Review:<br/><br/>Protagonists: After defeating the wicked School Master, our heroes went on to what was supposed to be their last Ever After, a happy one this time, for all involved, but when one story closes another begins. While Agatha and Sophie do feature heavily in this story, as well as everyone's favorite Coven of witches, this is very much Tedros's story. As Tedros becomes King of Camelot, the head that wears the crown is heavy indeed as Camelot is far from its Golden Age and is practically in sha</span>
  <span id="freeText16249003575379962937" style="display:none">Review:<br /><br />Protagonists: After defeating the wicked School Master, our heroes went on to what was supposed to be their last Ever After, a happy one this time, for all involved, but when one story closes another begins. While Agatha and Sophie do feature heavily in this story, as well as everyone's favorite Coven of witches, this is very much Tedros's story. As Tedros becomes King of Camelot, the head that wears the crown is heavy indeed as Camelot is far from its Golden Age and is practically in shambles. Being king isn't quite what Tedros expected and when a new evil surfaces and seems to be gunning for Tedros and his friends, things become even more complicated. I love these characters so much, even Sophie most of the time, and this book doesn't exactly treat them too kindly. However, I sort of wouldn't want it any other way, these characters have to go through challenges and trials otherwise their (presumed) victory at the end of the series wouldn't feel earned and neither would their character development. The first trilogy really only dealt with certain flaws that these characters have, usually one or two per person, but people don't usually only have one or two flaws and so more character development is necessary for this new trilogy, Tedros's impulsiveness and over protectiveness, Agatha's need to control things, and Sophie's hubris and jealousy, okay Sophie's flaws aren't that new, but they weren't really resolved in the last trilogy either. <br /><br />Romance: Much like the previous books in this series there isn't a TON of romance in this book, at least not compared to most YA books, but the for the amount there is, it sure makes an impact. With the annoying and aggravating love triangle finally, once and for all, behind them Agatha and Tedros are engaged and planning their wedding, however, royal duties and a new evil sort of stall that for the time being. Agatha and Tedros's romance has really only existed in times of war and when they're at peace, there can be some bumps in the road. I will say never once in this story did I doubt their love or even entertain the notion that by the end of this series they won't be together, but there are still some rough patches that they have to overcome, both personally and together, and while it's hard to watch them not be happy 100% of the time, I'm sure that by the end of this series they'll be all the stronger for it.<br /><br />World Building: Even though this was my MOST anticipated book for the year, I was a bit apprehensive toward it. In this age of reboots, revivals, and spin-offs, it's hard to know if a new or continued series in the same universe is what the author wants, what the publisher wants, what the readers want, or a combination of all three. I've read some series continuations that just feel like the author is dragging out the series for no good reason, luckily this isn't the case with this story. I wouldn't call it a continuation exactly, the original trilogy can stand by itself very easily, and this new trilogy has a very different vibe to the first one. It's darker and it goes places that the first trilogy didn't, that being said, while it feels more like a YA fantasy series, I do think it's still appropriate for the same age range as the first series, things are just more serious than they were before. We get to see more of the world, our characters have even greater responsibilities, and the villain they face is more cunning and manipulative than they've faced before. <br /><br />Predictability: I didn't know that much about this book going in, I didn't know who the new evil was, what it was after, I didn't even know what to expect in regards to the heroes that we saw seemingly having their Happily Ever Afters at the end of the previous book, because of that this book was pretty jarring. Unlike some people that I had seen that was excited about this book, I held no illusions that this would be a fluff book full of sunshine and rainbows, and yet I was still shocked at how dark this book got and how bleak it seemed at times. While most of this book was fairly unpredictable, there was one twist that I had theories about and being the ever inquisitive person I am, I sort of read the ending to see if I was right, I was FYI, and since that moment, every bit of foreshadowing felt like another log added to the fire and while I can't comment on how predictable this twist is, I will warn you against reading ahead. NO GOOD COMES FROM READING AHEAD!<br /><br />Ending: I'm not talking about the ending to this book. I can't, everytime I try to I ruin the ending, or at the very least I can see someone seeing through my vague words to the truth within. I'm just going to say this, the ending is intense, things happen, and I can't wait for book 5.<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />This was my most anticipated book of the year, and it did not disappoint. Sure, it broke me, it chewed me up and spit me out and left me desperate for the next installment, but I can see why the author guided the story in the way that he did, on the one hand, I respect him for taking this story in such a bold direction, and on the other hand I'm cursing his name with every fiber of my being... no joke.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16249003575379962937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6z1Kc8e4uIELe5Nm0qZK4Z2NTNmPNFi/RsVJvECZWbooZY1T+xwmizr5EbdGt/Ut7Am0MsfLMqFG0+dWjQ4/xA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TNJ3WbnvCp/yXI7hdDgV37nYh66lAXd6iPIQcDEGvUKPirB5hUuUlcPeDDDgKaoTyFx/Re3+HWSI5L6a/JHbPA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10419591151674040576">Soman Chainani's first novel, THE SCHOOL FOR GOOD AND EVIL, debuted on the New York Times Bestseller List, has been translated into 26 languages across six continents, and will soon be a major motion picture from Universal Studios. <br/><br/>The sequels, A WORLD WITHOUT PRINCES and THE LAST EVER AFTER, debuted on the New York Times Bestseller List as well. Together, the books of the series have been on the </span>
  <span id="freeText10419591151674040576" style="display:none">Soman Chainani's first novel, THE SCHOOL FOR GOOD AND EVIL, debuted on the New York Times Bestseller List, has been translated into 26 languages across six continents, and will soon be a major motion picture from Universal Studios. <br /><br />The sequels, A WORLD WITHOUT PRINCES and THE LAST EVER AFTER, debuted on the New York Times Bestseller List as well. Together, the books of the series have been on the print and extended NYT lists for a total of 33 weeks.<br /><br />As a writer and film director, Soman's films have played at over 150 film festivals around the world, winning more than 30 jury and audience prizes, and his writing awards include honors from Big Bear Lake, New Draft, the CAPE Foundation, the Sun Valley Writer’s Fellowship, and the coveted Shasha Grant, awarded by a jury of international film executives. <br /><br />When he’s not telling stories or teaching in New York City, Soman is a die-hard tennis player who never lost a first-round match for ten years . . . until he started writing THE SCHOOL FOR GOOD AND EVIL. Now he loses all the time.<br /></span>
